## Description

I used [this site](https://patorjk.com/software/taag/#p=display&f=3x5&t=Type%20Something%20) to make some ASCII art to save my super awesome flag, but something happened and all the spaces got deleted and I lost it. Luckily, I do remember that the MD5 hash of my flag was `a7bf5f833c3e4ceff2e006ff801ec16b`, so maybe you can help me.

Author: sy1vi3

The site was [https://patorjk.com/software/taag/#p=display&f=3x5&t=Type%20Something%20](https://patorjk.com/software/taag/#p=display&f=3x5&t=Type%20Something%20)

This is a site, where you can type text into a textbox, and then ASCII art depicting the text is output.

The challenge also gave you a txt file containing the text:

## Solution

I started out by creating a text file that contained every possible character that could be in the flag. The character order here is: `1234567890QWERTYUIOPASFGHJKLZXCVBNMqwertyuiopasdfghjklzxcvbnm!@#$%^&*()_+-=[]{};:,./<>`

And the text file text was:

```text
 #  ### ### # # ### ### ### ### ### ###  #  # # ### ##  ### # # # # ###  #  ##   #   ## ###  ## # #  ## # # #   ### # #  ## # # ##  ### # #                  #           #                    #  ##     #    #  #    #                  #            #  ### # #  ## # #  #   #   #    # #                    ## ##   ## ##                    #   # #   
##    #   # # # #   #     # # # # # # # # # # # #   # #  #  # # # #  #  # # # # # # #   #   #   # #   # # # #     # # # #   # # # # # # ### ### # # ### ### ### # # # #     ### ###  ##  ## ###  #  ### ###     # #  #  ##  # # ### # # ### ##  ###  #  # # ### ##    # # # #   ###  #   #       #      ###  #   #   #   #   #   #            #  #   #  
 #  ###  ## ### ### ###   # ### ### # # # # ### ##  ##   #   #  # #  #  # # ##  ###  #  ##  # # ###   # ##  #    #   #  #   # # ##  # # ### # # ### ##  #    #  ### # #  #  # # # # # #  #  # # ### # # # #  #  ##   #   #   #  #   # # # # # # ###  #  #   # # ###  #       ##  #   #   #      ### ###      #   #  ##   ##                  #  #     # 
 #  #     #   #   # # #   # # #   # # #  ## ### #   # #  #   #  # #  #  # # #   # #   # #   # # # # # # # # #   #   # # #   # # # # # # # # ### ### ### #    ##   # ###  ## ### ### ### ##  ###  #   ## # #  #  # #  ##  ## # # ###  #  ### # # # #     ### ###  ## #       # # ###  #   #       #      ###  #   #   #   #   #   #   #      #    #   #  
### ### ###   # ### ###   # ### ### ###   # # # ### # #  #   #  ### ###  #  #   # # ##  #    ## # #  #  # # ### ### # #  ##  #  ##  # # # #   #                 ###             #               ##  ###     #                                        #      # # ##  # #     ###  #    # #   ###              ## ##   ## ##  #       #    #  #     # # 
```

I then wrote some python code that isolated each individual character, stripped all the whitespace from it and then combined it with every other possible character in every combination in order to get a list of every possible two letter combination these characters can form:

{% raw %}

```python
from itertools import product

# File path
filename = "character_sheet.txt"

# Original known character set
original_chars = "1234567890QWERTYUIOPASFGHJKLZXCVBNMqwertyuiopasdfghjklzxcvbnm!@#$%^&*()_+-=[]{};:,./<>"

# Constants
CHAR_WIDTH = 4   # Width of each character block in ASCII art
CHAR_HEIGHT = 5  # Height of each character block

# Step 1: Read ASCII art from file
with open(filename, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
	lines = [line.rstrip("\n") for line in f.readlines()]

# Step 2: Split ASCII into individual characters
ascii_letters = []
num_chars = len(lines[0]) // CHAR_WIDTH

for i in range(num_chars):
	letter_block = []
	for row in range(CHAR_HEIGHT):
		start = i * CHAR_WIDTH
		end = start + CHAR_WIDTH
		letter_block.append(lines[row][start:end])
	ascii_letters.append("\n".join(letter_block))

# Step 3: remove whitespace from ascii_letters
ascii_letters = [letter.replace(" ", "") for letter in ascii_letters]

# Step 4: Map each ASCII character to the original character
single_char_map = dict(zip(original_chars, ascii_letters))

# Step 5: Generate all two-letter combinations (including same letter)
two_letter_combos = ["".join(pair) for pair in product(original_chars, repeat=2)]

# Step 6: Add together the ascii Art
combo_ascii_letters = []
for combo in two_letter_combos:
	ascii_combo_tuple_tuple = zip(single_char_map[combo[0]].split("\n"), single_char_map[combo[1]].split("\n"))
	ascii_combo_list_str = ["".join(i) for i in ascii_combo_tuple_tuple]
	combo_ascii_letters.append([combo, "\n".join(ascii_combo_list_str)])

# Step 7: print out result in order to copy into a brute forcing python file
print(combo_ascii_letters)
```

This printed out

I then wrote a python script that allows me to print in the `flag.txt` file's text and then it outputs all the possible combinations that these characters could be:

['>P', '###\n###\n###\n##\n##'], ['>A', '##\n###\n####\n###\n###'], ['>S', '###\n##\n##\n##\n###'], ['>F', '####\n##\n###\n##\n##'], ['>G', '###\n##\n###\n###\n###'], ['>H', ['>C', '###\n##\n##\n##\n###'], ['>V', '###\n###\n###\n###\n##'], ['>B', '###\n###\n###\n###\n###'], ['>N', '####\n###\n###\n###\n###'], ['>M', '###\n####\n####\n###\n###'], ['>q', '#\n####\n###\n####\n##'], ['>w', '#\n###\n####\n####\n#'], ['>e', '#\n####\n###\n####\n#'], ['>r', '#\n####\n##\n##\n#'], ['>t', '##\n####\n##\n###\n#'], ['>y', '#\n###\n####\n##\n####'], ['>u', '#\n###\n###\n####\n#'], ['>i', '##\n#\n##\n###\n#'], ['>o', '#\n####\n###\n####\n#'], ['>p', '#\n####\n###\n####\n##'], ['>a', '#\n###\n###\n####\n#'], ['>s', '#\n###\n##\n###\n#'], ['>d', '##\n####\n###\n####\n#'], ['>f', '###\n##\n####\n##\n###'], ['>g', '#\n####\n###\n###\n####'], ['>h', '##\n####\n###\n###\n#'], ['>j', '##\n#\n##\n##\n##'], ['>k', '##\n###\n###\n###\n#'], ['>l', '##\n##\n##\n###\n#'], ['>z', '#\n###\n##\n###\n#'], ['>x', '#\n###\n##\n###\n#'], ['>c', '#\n####\n##\n####\n#'], ['>v', '#\n###\n###\n##\n#'], ['>b', '##\n####\n###\n####\n#'], ['>n', '#\n###\n###\n###\n#'], ['>m', '#\n####\n####\n###\n#'], ['>!', '##\n##\n##\n#\n##'], ['>@', '####\n###\n##\n####\n#'], ['>#', '###\n####\n###\n####\n###'], ['>$', '###\n###\n####\n###\n###'], ['>%', '###\n##\n##\n##\n###'], ['>^', '##\n###\n#\n#\n#'], ['>&', '##\n##\n###\n###\n####'], ['>*', '##\n####\n##\n####\n##'], ['>(', '##\n##\n##\n##\n##'], ['>)', '##\n##\n##\n##\n##'], ['>_', '#\n#\n#\n#\n####'], ['>+', '#\n##\n####\n##\n#'], ['>-', '#\n#\n####\n#\n#'], ['>=', '#\n####\n#\n####\n#'], ['>[', '###\n##\n##\n##\n###'], ['>]', '###\n##\n##\n##\n###'], ['>{', '###\n##\n###\n##\n###'], ['>}', '###\n##\n###\n##\n###'], ['>;', '#\n##\n#\n##\n##'], ['>:', '#\n##\n#\n##\n#'], ['>,', '#\n#\n#\n##\n##'], ['>.', '#\n#\n#\n#\n##'], ['>/', '##\n##\n##\n##\n##'], ['><', '##\n##\n##\n##\n##'], ['>>', '##\n##\n##\n##\n##']]

```python
chars = []

char = ""

while True:
	while True:
		inp = input().strip()
		if inp == "": break
		char += "\n" + inp

	chars.append(char[1:])
	
	char = ""
	
	e = input().strip()
	if e == "no": break
	else: char = "\n" + e

print(chars)

possible_results = [[] for i in range(len(chars))]
for i, char in enumerate(chars):
	for c in combos:
		testing_against = c[1].strip()
		if testing_against == char.strip():
			possible_results[i] += [c[0]]
			
print(possible_results)
```

This python program when I inputed in the entire `flag.txt` files content, printed out:

```text
[['3L', 'EL', 'L3', 'LE'], ['2q', '2p', '5q', '5p', 'RA', 'AR', 'AK', 'AB', 'KA', 'BA', 'q2', 'q5', 'p2', 'p5'], ['j{', 'j}', '{j', '}j'], ['us', 'uz', 'ux', 'as', 'az', 'ax', 'su', 'sa', 'zu', 'za', 'xu', 'xa'], ['7_', 'T_', 'I.', 'Z.', '_7', '_T', '.I', '.Z'], ['4q', '4p', 'Rm', 'Ah', 'Km', 'Bm', 'Mn', 'q4', 'p4', 'hA', 'nM', 'mR', 'mK', 'mB'], ['tt'], ['3r', 'Er', 'r3', 'rE'], ['n_', '_n'], ['4m', 'm4'], ['tc', 'h=', 'ct', '=h'], ['1h', 'Ur', 'rU', 'h1'], ['yc', 'gn', 'cy', 'ng'], ['4_', '_4'], ['1:', 't_', '_t', ':1'], ['1f', 'f1'], ['rs', 'rz', 'rx', 'sr', 'zr', 'xr'], ['7_', 'T_', 'I.', 'Z.', '_7', '_T', '.I', '.Z'], ['ud', 'ub', 'ad', 'ab', 'du', 'da', 'bu', 'ba'], ['7_', 'T_', 'I.', 'Z.', '_7', '_T', '.I', '.Z'], ['th', 'ht'], ['2s', '2z', '2x', '3n', '5s', '5z', '5x', 'Q{', 'Q}', 'W!', 'En', 'O{', 'O}', 'H(', 'H)', 'H/', 'H<', 'H>', 'Mj', 's2', 's5', 'jM', 'z2', 'z5', 'x2', 'x5', 'n3', 'nE', '!W', '$(', '$)', '$/', '$<', '$>', '(H', '($', ')H', ')$', '{Q', '{O', '}Q', '}O', '/H', '/$', '<H', '<$', '>H', '>$'], ['y_', '_y'], ['6c', '0u', '0a', 'u0', 'a0', 'c6'], ['n_', '_n'], ['2I', '2Z', '33', '3E', '5I', '5Z', 'E3', 'EE', 'I2', 'I5', 'Z2', 'Z5'], ['Ls', 'Lz', 'Lx', 'sL', 'd_', 'zL', 'xL', 'b_', '_d', '_b'], ['4_', '_4'], ['2t', '3h', '4X', '5t', 'Eh', 'RP', 'YH', 'Y$', 'PR', 'PK', 'PB', 'HY', 'KP', 'X4', 'BP', 't2', 't5', 'h3', 'hE', '$Y'], ['ru', 'ra', 'ur', 'ar', 'cv', 'vc'], ['1s', '1z', '1x', 's1', 'z1', 'x1'], ['1t', 't1'], ['c_', '_c'], ['0t', 'Y#', 't0', '#Y'], ['n_', '_n'], ['4r', 'r4'], ['0r', 'r0'], ['w_', '_w'], ['1t', 't1'], ['Ls', 'Lz', 'Lx', 'sL', 'd_', 'zL', 'xL', 'b_', '_d', '_b'], ['6e', '6o', '8u', '8a', '0w', 'QW', 'WQ', 'WO', 'OW', 'w0', 'e6', 'u8', 'o6', 'a8'], ['Gv', 'X+', 'sf', 'fs', 'fz', 'fx', 'zf', 'xf', 'vG', 'n{', 'n}', '+X', '{n', '}n']]
```

Now its time to brute force, the only problem is that this array gets over 6 octillion different combinations for what the flag could be. Now I don't have the computing power, or time to do that many combinations, this was a 2 day CTF, and I did this challenge on day 2.

So, let's see if we can instead do some estimated guesses by assuming that the flag spells out something human readable in either english or 1337.

e.g. at the start we know it is `L3AK`, and then we know its a `{` so the combo is probably `{j`, then it looks like we can spell the word `jus7_` or `jusT_` afterwards.

Doing this for a while gets the much shorter list of possible values:

```text
[['L3'], ['AK'], ['{j'], ['us'], ['7_', 'T_'], ['p4'], ['tt'], ['3r', 'Er'], ['n_'], ['m4'], ['tc'], ['h1'], ['ng'], ['_4'], ['t_'], ['f1'], ['rs'], ['7_', 'T_'], ['bu'], ['7_', 'T_'], ['th'], ['3n', 'En'], ['_y'], ['0u'], ['_n'], ['33', '3E', 'E3', 'EE'], ['d_'], ['4_'], ['h3', 'hE'] , ['ur'], ['1s'], ['t1'], ['c_'], ['t0'], ['_n'], ['4r'], ['r0'], ['w_'], ['1t'], ['_d'], ['0w', 'OW'], ['n}']]
```

This results in a flag along the lines of `L3AK{jus7_p4ttern_m4tch1ng_4t_f1rst_but_then_y0u_need_4_heur1st1c_t0_n4rr0w_1t_down}`. which makes sense, now just time to get the exact characters, which is normally just if it is a capital letter, or a 1337 style number e.g. `need` could be `nEEd`, `nE3d`, `n3Ed`, or `n33d`

To solve this I made another python script that prints out every possible combination, and its MD5sum.

```python
# Probable probabilities
probabilities =  [['L3'], ['AK'], ['{j'], ['us'], ['7_', 'T_'], ['p4'], ['tt'], ['3r', 'Er'], ['n_'], ['m4'], ['tc'], ['h1'], ['ng'], ['_4'], ['t_'], ['f1'], ['rs'], ['7_', 'T_'], ['bu'], ['7_', 'T_'], ['th'], ['3n', 'En'], ['_y'], ['0u'], ['_n'], ['33', '3E', 'E3', 'EE'], ['d_'], ['4_'], ['h3', 'hE'] , ['ur'], ['1s'], ['t1'], ['c_'], ['t0'], ['_n'], ['4r'], ['r0'], ['w_'], ['1t'], ['_d'], ['0w', 'OW'], ['n}']]

# L3AK{jus7_p4tt3rn_m4tch1ng_4t_f1rs7_bu7_th3n_y0u_n33d_4_h3ur1st1c_t0_n4rr0w_1t_d0wn}
# a7bf5f833c3e4ceff2e006ff801ec16b

import hashlib
from itertools import product

for combo in product(*probabilities):
	full_string = "".join(combo)
	md5_sum = hashlib.md5(full_string.encode()).hexdigest()
	print(f"{full_string} : {md5_sum}")
```

I then ran the file and grepped it for the proper MD5sum, in order to get the flag:

```bash
$ python hasher.py | grep a7bf5f833c3e4ceff2e006ff801ec16b
L3AK{jus7_p4tt3rn_m4tch1ng_4t_f1rs7_bu7_th3n_y0u_n33d_4_h3ur1st1c_t0_n4rr0w_1t_d0wn} : a7bf5f833c3e4ceff2e006ff801ec16b
```

This gets us the flag of `L3AK{jus7_p4tt3rn_m4tch1ng_4t_f1rs7_bu7_th3n_y0u_n33d_4_h3ur1st1c_t0_n4rr0w_1t_d0wn}`

{% endraw %}
